  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4691dc53-ef7b-428e-a464-4b8f67b3487c'
      });

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119653562" />
    <a title="Phillip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1798592-phillip"><img alt="Phillip" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119653562?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phillip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phillip" href="/user/show/1798592-phillip">Phillip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119653562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7830589917722624372">This is my third effort at writing a review of the book. Obviously, it resists reviewing (at least by a 44 y.o. like myself).<br/><br/>I found this book, and the whole Emily the Strange phenomenon, by accident, while browsing in a used bookstore. I picked up a copy they had out on the shelf and started thumbing through it and was immediately hooked. The conceit of the book caught my attention, and three days later, I'd finished it (the book, not the conceit).<br/><br/>I found the book to be extremely enjoyable and </span>
  <span id="freeText7830589917722624372" style="display:none">This is my third effort at writing a review of the book. Obviously, it resists reviewing (at least by a 44 y.o. like myself).<br /><br />I found this book, and the whole Emily the Strange phenomenon, by accident, while browsing in a used bookstore. I picked up a copy they had out on the shelf and started thumbing through it and was immediately hooked. The conceit of the book caught my attention, and three days later, I'd finished it (the book, not the conceit).<br /><br />I found the book to be extremely enjoyable and quite compelling. I expected to be disappointed by the book; any book with more than one author (like any screenplay with more than one writing credit) is bound to be terrible. But the book is smart, well written, and, as one would expect from a novel coming out of the Emily the Strange milieu, very cleverly illustrated.<br /><br />As a 44 year old man, I would never have thought to have been caught dead with an Emily the Strange book in my hands. Having read it, while I may not rush out and put a EtS bumper sticker on my car, I'll buy the next book in the series and not worry quite as much about being seen with it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7830589917722624372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2689128802?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9556468-aly?shelf=2019">2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2689128802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18085038561689461874">Just like the title, this book is strange. The book starts with the main character having amnesia and not knowing where she is, who she is, or what's going on. She decides to call herself Earwig. Why?! So weird. And that pretty much sets the tone for the book. Crazy things happen, nothing really makes sense, even when you find out what's going on. The story is told through the main character's journal entries and she makes tons of lists which are kind of funny. The narrator was enthusiastic and </span>
  <span id="freeText18085038561689461874" style="display:none">Just like the title, this book is strange. The book starts with the main character having amnesia and not knowing where she is, who she is, or what's going on. She decides to call herself Earwig. Why?! So weird. And that pretty much sets the tone for the book. Crazy things happen, nothing really makes sense, even when you find out what's going on. The story is told through the main character's journal entries and she makes tons of lists which are kind of funny. The narrator was enthusiastic and did a pretty good job, although her teenage voices were odd. <br />I did like the story and was eager to find out answers to the various mysteries happening around Black Rock. I would read the sequels to see what other crazy things Emily gets in to and the strange people she meets. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18085038561689461874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_90944698" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90944698" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3329762-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505246119p2/3329762.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90944698?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/3329762-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90944698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16590367232886187868">13 Elements you will find in the first Emily the Strange novel:<br/>1. Mystery<br/>2. A beautiful golem<br/>3. Souped-up slingshots<br/>4. Four black cats<br/>5. Amnesia<br/>6. Calamity Poker<br/>7. Angry ponies<br/>8. A shady truant officer<br/>9. Top-13 lists<br/>10. A sandstorm generator<br/>11. Doppelgängers<br/>12. A secret mission<br/>13. Earwigs<br/>Emily the Strange: 13 years old. Able to leap tall buildings, probably, if she felt like it. More likely to be napping with her four black cats; or cobbling together a particle accelerator out of lint, lentils, </span>
  <span id="freeText16590367232886187868" style="display:none">13 Elements you will find in the first Emily the Strange novel:<br />1. Mystery<br />2. A beautiful golem<br />3. Souped-up slingshots<br />4. Four black cats<br />5. Amnesia<br />6. Calamity Poker<br />7. Angry ponies<br />8. A shady truant officer<br />9. Top-13 lists<br />10. A sandstorm generator<br />11. Doppelgängers<br />12. A secret mission<br />13. Earwigs<br />Emily the Strange: 13 years old. Able to leap tall buildings, probably, if she felt like it. More likely to be napping with her four black cats; or cobbling together a particle accelerator out of lint, lentils, and safety pins; or rocking out on drums/ guitar/saxophone/zither; or painting a swirling feral sewer mural; or forcing someone to say "swirling feral sewer mural" 13 times fast . . . and pointing and laughing.<br /><br />4 words: I. LOVED. THIS. BOOK.<br /><br />Emily the Strange: The Lost Days is told completely through diary entries by Emily-- or Earwig as she calls herself in the book. The overall voice and tone of the book is entertaining and generally hilarious. The cover is kind of misleading, because looking at it makes one think it the book is a gloom and doom goth book. But DON’T BE FOOLED! This book is so funny and enjoyable, and seriously, not at all as dark as it seems.<br /><br />I was very surprised by this book. I didn’t take it as seriously as an actual novel, but it actually had great characters and plot that really threw me for a loop. I love Emily (Earwig) as a character. She was just so spunky. I really had a great time being inside her head. She makes up the funniest curse words and slang. (NOTE: There is no actually cursing. Just funny words.)<br /><br />One of my favorite parts of this whole novel were the drawings on almost every page. They added a different perspective to the reading experience, and really brought the novel to life.<br /><br />This was a much lighter read than I’m used to, but still totally enjoyable. 5 stars!<br /><br />Review from "What's Your Story? YA Book Reviews":<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://whatsyourstorybookreviews.blogspot.com/">http://whatsyourstorybookreviews.blog...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16590367232886187868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1277291723689767999">Ahoy there mateys! I absolutely loved this audiobook! It was narrated by Angela Goethals. This book is so funny and awesome. I knew it was for me just based on the cover. I can’t really summarize the zany plot in any articulate fashion. I cannot do this justice. I must read the rest of the series. A</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258565768?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AennA" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AennA" href="/user/show/7339302-aenna">AennA</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258565768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1092058927743076779">The first of the four released books under Emily the Strange series, The Lost Days, tells us the story of Emily Strange finding herself in a place she doesn't know, and remembering nothing about herself. All she have are her pen and notebook, which remained her buddy pieces. <br/><br/>She eventually learned she's in a town called Blackrock, as she saw in a newspaper, and tried to find the truth on what happened to her. Still remembering nothing about her past, or her present she roamed around Blackrock an</span>
  <span id="freeText1092058927743076779" style="display:none">The first of the four released books under Emily the Strange series, The Lost Days, tells us the story of Emily Strange finding herself in a place she doesn't know, and remembering nothing about herself. All she have are her pen and notebook, which remained her buddy pieces. <br /><br />She eventually learned she's in a town called Blackrock, as she saw in a newspaper, and tried to find the truth on what happened to her. Still remembering nothing about her past, or her present she roamed around Blackrock and found different personalities, which helped her complete the puzzle on what's really happening to her. <br /><br />Reading this, I am as confused as the character, Emily Strange. There are some scenarios that doesn't seem to fit the story, which I would to like believe is intentionally done by the author. Different characters bring in different puzzle pieces and eventually the story was complete and it brought a fresh kind of adventure for Emily.<br /><br />I read this book after reading the 3rd book, so I already know who Emily Strange is, and how she functions as a character. I am delighted with the book's layout, with quirky artworks and witty details. The funky design adds up to the delightful experience of finishing the story.<br /><br />Emily is indeed a strange and smart girl, and you'll be amazed how she handles some scenarios. Join Emily as she unravels the truth on why she can't remember anything, and what is she doing in Blackrock.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1092058927743076779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10274873375136798062">2.5 Felt an odd amount of nostalgia for a book I have never read before. I read this on my kindle and checked it out after confusing it with a popular graphic novel I see people talk about quite a bit here. What am I thinking of??? It´s driving me nuts.<br/><br/>The writing felt a bit forced (like a middle aged man trying to sound like a 13 year old moody girl...which I suppose IS the case actually) but I did really fall for the story and especially the strange Little setting of BlackRock.   <span id="freeText10274873375136798062" style="display:none">2.5 Felt an odd amount of nostalgia for a book I have never read before. I read this on my kindle and checked it out after confusing it with a popular graphic novel I see people talk about quite a bit here. What am I thinking of??? It´s driving me nuts.<br /><br />The writing felt a bit forced (like a middle aged man trying to sound like a 13 year old moody girl...which I suppose IS the case actually) but I did really fall for the story and especially the strange Little setting of BlackRock. I won´t continue with the series, but it was a cute Little read. I´m sure slightly emo me would have adored this series growing up.<br /><br />Also,apologiges if there are ample typos here. I´m typing this on my school´s computer which only understands Spanish, so this whole thing looks like one giant typo. </span>

<div id="review_3022645699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3022645699" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104452716-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3022645699?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/104452716-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3022645699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14998585988885895560">“Emily the Strange: The Lost Days” by Rob Reger is a fantasy book about a "miserable" girl named Emily who has amnesia and is lost in a small town by the name of “Black Rock.” She is on a journey to try to find out her biological family and remember her OWN name. I recommend this book to kids who like dark and weird stuff because Emily is (obviously) strange and she talks about negative stuff about people and the world. She also likes talking about black magic or ritual stuff. I really liked thi</span>
  <span id="freeText14998585988885895560" style="display:none">“Emily the Strange: The Lost Days” by Rob Reger is a fantasy book about a "miserable" girl named Emily who has amnesia and is lost in a small town by the name of “Black Rock.” She is on a journey to try to find out her biological family and remember her OWN name. I recommend this book to kids who like dark and weird stuff because Emily is (obviously) strange and she talks about negative stuff about people and the world. She also likes talking about black magic or ritual stuff. I really liked this book because I thought that this book was different than other ones. I’ve never read a book whose main character has an interest in evil or a kid who has memory loss and I just thought it was really cool to make a character like that. I don’t really recommend this book to people who hate or dislike negative people or stuff because Emily is completely the opposite of positive. She rarely likes to smile, she talks about black magic, she has low self esteem, and she wears all black (which according to some people that’s negative). But unless you can handle her negativity, you’ll be just fine! But even though she might be negative, she can be pretty funny and relatable in a way. Otherwise, I do like this book and recommend it to kids or people who love dark stuff.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14998585988885895560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1165911808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1650984594422903279">13 Elements you'll find in the book<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459312317i/18594013._SY540_.jpg' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I've had this book for more than 5 years and I still re-read it from time to time!<br/><br/>Emily lost her memory and she finds her self sitting on a bench in a park (more of a patch of grass really) located in a beige coloured town. <div id="review_62209518" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62209518" />
    <a title="Lindsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/664635-lindsey"><img alt="Lindsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442475355p2/664635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62209518?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey" href="/user/show/664635-lindsey">Lindsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62209518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer47650173954816172">I had only heard of Emily The Strange in passing, and didn’t really know much about the books, comics, or product line. However, I’m already in love with the character and the way the stories are told. It reminds me of a very intelligent version of Greg Heffley from the Diary of a Wimpy Kid series, except that instead of it being almost entirely graphic novel, it's part novel, part graphics, and part a whole bunch of other interesting stuff. In a way, it’s similar to the process through which th</span>
  <span id="freeText47650173954816172" style="display:none">I had only heard of Emily The Strange in passing, and didn’t really know much about the books, comics, or product line. However, I’m already in love with the character and the way the stories are told. It reminds me of a very intelligent version of Greg Heffley from the Diary of a Wimpy Kid series, except that instead of it being almost entirely graphic novel, it's part novel, part graphics, and part a whole bunch of other interesting stuff. In a way, it’s similar to the process through which the Objectivist poets like William Carlos Williams in Patterson and Louis Zukofsky in A would compose a book-length poem that was comprised of a motley mixture of various elements, like some of their own work with newspaper clippings, letters, posters, ads, and all sorts of other treasures. <br /><br />Aside from the composition of the novel, the story itself is also engaging. Unlike the normal progression of most stories, which starts at the beginning and moves through to the end, you get the sense that you’ve picked up somewhere in the middle. This is especially evidenced by the fact that you start on diary page 13. Thus, you are on the amnesiac ride along with Emily the entire time. What makes this particularly clever and interesting as a twist to the story is that, in reality, the whole point of the story is shifted. You think it’s about Emily’s quest to get her memory back, when it’s actually about something else entirely, which you can only discover as she uncovers it.<br /><br />This has quickly become one of my new favorite books, and I’ve recommended it to several people already. It’s a great read for anyone with an afternoon free, but its target age will be 9-13 year olds.<br /><br />-Lindsey Miller, <a href="http://www.lindseyslibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.lindseyslibrary.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="47650173954816172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_544249684" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/544249684" />
    <a title="Jamila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2963642-jamila"><img alt="Jamila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434268418p2/2963642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/544249684?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamila" href="/user/show/2963642-jamila">Jamila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer544249684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9494105905266645120">Emily doesn't know she's called Emily. She doesn't know anyone else's name. She doesn't know why she can't remember these things, or why eleven pages were torn out of her notebook. But she knows that she must figure out who she is, and why this happened to her.<br/><br/>This is the first book in the series, and it begins well enough to keep you turning the pages for most of it; from the moment you start reading, you join Emily; you want to know how she got to where she is - in life, and on the bench where</span>
  <span id="freeText9494105905266645120" style="display:none">Emily doesn't know she's called Emily. She doesn't know anyone else's name. She doesn't know why she can't remember these things, or why eleven pages were torn out of her notebook. But she knows that she must figure out who she is, and why this happened to her.<br /><br />This is the first book in the series, and it begins well enough to keep you turning the pages for most of it; from the moment you start reading, you join Emily; you want to know how she got to where she is - in life, and on the bench where she is sitting. However, towards the middle, I find that the story gets a little boring; she doesn't learn much about herself, and she doesn't do much apart from walk around the small town in which she finds herself. Also, near the end, the story suddenly gets a little bit complicated, so that you have to read carefully to understand what is going on.<br /><br />Still, this is a fairly quick read, and I love the way the author doesn't get tied down by trying to make it realistic. There are a lot of things in here that could in no way happen in real life (Unless you are talking philosophically or being very pedantic - which I am not at the moment!), like how no-one tries to help Emily find somewhere safe to stay, and how she always knows what to do. These things make you WANT to read, rather than put down the book.<br /><br />Emily really isn't your stereotype teenage girl; she doesn't do predictable things like wear pink and worry about what people think about her. No, she's an original character-- one I wish I could have invented.<br /><br />This book would probably appeal to people aged nine or ten and above, and to both boys and girls.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9494105905266645120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_103536718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103536718" />
    <a title="mina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/725750-mina"><img alt="mina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199013179p2/725750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103536718?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mina" href="/user/show/725750-mina">mina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103536718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16819192327988192703">It is a book written by an amnesiac girl (whom we already knew as Emily, since it was written in big red colour on the cover, duh!). She found herself sitting on a super-mini-park bench, totally in amnesia, equipped only with a slingshot, a pen, and a blank black book. She didn't know her own name, didn't know the name of the town she was in, didn't know what she did there. But it seemed that she knew many unusual things, such as repair anything broken (including golems), how to throw stones acc</span>
  <span id="freeText16819192327988192703" style="display:none">It is a book written by an amnesiac girl (whom we already knew as Emily, since it was written in big red colour on the cover, duh!). She found herself sitting on a super-mini-park bench, totally in amnesia, equipped only with a slingshot, a pen, and a blank black book. She didn't know her own name, didn't know the name of the town she was in, didn't know what she did there. But it seemed that she knew many unusual things, such as repair anything broken (including golems), how to throw stones accurately, and how to play Calamity Poker (after watching the game for some time, while others have to do some bloody ritual first, and learn it for years, before understand the rules). She lived in a refrigerator box, behind a cafe named El Dungeon, a very unusual grey place, with Raven as the dim-witted barrista, who couldn't say a complete sentence, but she made very delicious sandwiches.<br /><br />Was there any reason she was there? Who made her amnesia? How come Raven was never sleep? Why there were no trees but the one in the mini-park? Why everything was painted grey? Why her parents didn't look for her? And lotsa lotsa questions, one by one will be answered at the end of the book.<br /><br />Some pages in the book was ripped (by Emily herself) for some reasons. Of course, you can read the ripped pages at the end of the book, but it would spoil the story. <br /><br />I have liked Emily's character since I saw her on t-shirt, and after finding out in this book that she was so singular, makes me even like her more. Would go buy the second book: Stranger &amp; Stranger. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="16819192327988192703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_70586696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70586696" />
    <a title="Alisha Marie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1585205-alisha-marie"><img alt="Alisha Marie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555610435p2/1585205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70586696?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alisha Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alisha Marie" href="/user/show/1585205-alisha-marie">Alisha Marie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1585205-alisha-marie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70586696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6892122685944915112">My first foray into Emily Strange happened when I saw a drawing of her on the computer once. So, I got the inspiration to write a short story based on this character (based solely on her looks and name, didn't know any of her history) for an English assignment. It all worked out, got an A+ on the assignment and have been an Emily Strange fan ever since. Even owning an Emily Strange graphic tee and wallet.<br/><br/>That's why I wanted to like this book so much. I took the book out of the library instead of</span>
  <span id="freeText6892122685944915112" style="display:none">My first foray into Emily Strange happened when I saw a drawing of her on the computer once. So, I got the inspiration to write a short story based on this character (based solely on her looks and name, didn't know any of her history) for an English assignment. It all worked out, got an A+ on the assignment and have been an Emily Strange fan ever since. Even owning an Emily Strange graphic tee and wallet.<br /><br />That's why I wanted to like this book so much. I took the book out of the library instead of buying it because I wasn't so sure how the whole story would work out. While I liked the premise of the book, a lot of tended to be repetitive. Emily gets amnesia, writes notes in her notebook trying to figure out the whole sordid detail, rinse, wash, and repeat. Still, I started enjoying it more towards the middle. Emily is a very likeable heroine. Really witty and sarcastic, something that I love. I still think I would've liked this book more had I been a bit younger.<br /><br />So, anyway, I give this book three stars. It was cute and had an intriguing mystery (plus intriguing heroine and intriguing supporting characters), but it wasn't too deep. Besides that, I'm actually looking forward to the second installment in the Emily Strange series, although, they will be library reads as I have no desire to own them (although I would love to own some of the artwork since it's pretty kick-ass).<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6892122685944915112" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7230604899829494151" style="display:none">I admit it - I'm old and was never hip so a lot of pop culture stuff passes me by without even stopping to say hello. I didn't know who or what Emily the Strange was, but in this book, neither does she. It turns out Emily started as a sort of anitdote to Hello Kitty - appealing to those goth and wannabe goth teens who are too cool for that perky white cat. <br />So then Emily started appearing not only on tee shirts, but in some graphic novel/comic books, too. And now she is the star of a series of novels aimed at middle schoolers. And if she doesn't catch on with the underground cool kids in middle school, there is no justice in the world. <br />Her first adventure is truly bizarre, wacko, fun and, well, strange. But I loved it. Like I said, I've always been too nerdy to be cool, but if I could go back in time, I'd love to be Emily. Except maybe with dogs instead of cats.<br />Emily wakes up to find she doesn't know who she is or where she is. But she makes friends with some cats and with a "girl" who works in a coffee shop. She also makes friends with a sideshow attraction who can read minds. As she tries to track down who and where she is, she starts piecing together a strange story that is too complicated to explain. Suffice it to say it involves dead relatives, a golem, the town council, and a mysterious black rock. <br />Read this and for a few hours, you feel pretty darn cool - in a 13-yr-old goth girl sort of way.</span>

And I love the fact that the authors included the ripped out pages from the front and middle of the book. They even kept the page numbers on them!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  <span id="freeText2751619157217292207" style="display:none">Okay, this book was adorable. I'll admit, at first it was a little difficult for me to get into. In fact, I almost put it down.   <span id="freeText13334289353242614140" style="display:none"><br />REVIEW<br /><br />Emily does strange, but she does strange funny. She is sarcastic and smart – she asks quirky questions and has crazy conversations. She doodles and draws – she is random and resourceful. The mystery goes back around 100 years and it was a complete surprise to me. <br /><br />This book is packed with humor, fun, and mystery.   <span id="freeText1986420401452652457" style="display:none">I had such mixed feelings about this book while I was reading it. I've had two of these books for a while now and have been wanting to read them for so long. I really enjoyed the pictures in the book, but as I was reading, I was starting to wonder if I was supposed to know more about Emily as a character before reading these. I think there are also Emily the Strange graphic novels that came out before the regular novels. I knew that before I started reading the novels and figured it wouldn't matter, but then about halfway through, I thought perhaps it would matter. But as the story started coming to an end, I realized that it didn't matter, everything started making sense.<br /><br />I enjoyed this first novel adaptation. Emily is a fun character, and I really enjoyed all her fun little "swear" words. The magical element was fun and interesting, and now I'm excited to see what could happen next, since it seems like that the end was really the end and there wasn't room for a sequel. I'm not sure if I'll check out the graphic novels or not, for now I look forward to the remaining novels.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11050643962406665944">I've always wanted to read this ever since I got a charm bracelet of it, and it was my luck that my college friend had it.<br/><br/>I gave this 5 stars, because I read it in one sitting.   <span id="freeText11050643962406665944" style="display:none">I've always wanted to read this ever since I got a charm bracelet of it, and it was my luck that my college friend had it.<br /><br />I gave this 5 stars, because I read it in one sitting. I couldn't stop reading it, because of the constant mystery, randomness, and awesomeness the author had written. Not to mention, the illustration was very interesting also.<br /><br />The story is about a girl who woke up with nothing but a few items in hand, and no memory at all. There were also cats, golems, and LISTS. With those, anyone who picked up this book would already be hooked. The writing style was also very casual(because it was supposed to be her diary)--and yet, intellectual. The characters were all interesting and the author did a good job in making Emily the smart and quirky teenager everyone would love to read about.<br /><br />I was also surprised by the twists and turns in this awesome book, and I'm really glad I got to read it.<br /><br />Kudos to Rob Reger and Jessica Gruner! I can't wait to read the next one. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11050643962406665944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer228488412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14187816232586015423">Ugh this was supposed to be a good book! But of course I’m asking for too much.<br/><br/>I admit that I got this only because I’m in love with Emily and I felt ashamed for never actually reading one of her books. Plus our Goodreads group’s main image is of Emily. I like to have some insight on the stuff I use, you know.<br/><br/>So, what did I like? Emily’s sarcasm, the writing style, the book’s layout and all the cool images scattered all around.<br/><br/>What I didn’t like and what actually made me give it up? <b>Boredom</b>.Too </span>
  <span id="freeText14187816232586015423" style="display:none">Ugh this was supposed to be a good book! But of course I’m asking for too much.<br /><br />I admit that I got this only because I’m in love with Emily and I felt ashamed for never actually reading one of her books. Plus our Goodreads group’s main image is of Emily. I like to have some insight on the stuff I use, you know.<br /><br />So, what did I like? Emily’s sarcasm, the writing style, the book’s layout and all the cool images scattered all around.<br /><br />What I didn’t like and what actually made me give it up? <b>Boredom</b>.Too much freakin’ boredom. I’m sorry but the story is not for me. I don’t know if it’s this book or the series itself, and frankly I’m not tempted to try another one, but the story is (forgive the pun) strange.<br /><br />Soooo DNF my dear Emily. Things can never work out between us.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Fy5ee3Ni7dnMu7S9RA20cQcpg9MUStk8poK6idqA1y9v1e0cVEN+DEnF0rBREqrAumTteKxRUAmony5DJChBgg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bYKYFGkASPQdjFezeV0o+W32Tzrqca/WKBCYFjWWWBwVeStzTiHbIZjyMb5sQjZI0LshkVJqJuMmDQzcyz7OsQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17480271672416818897">Reger's friend Nathan Carrico designed Emily in 1991 for a skateboard company in Santa Cruz, where Cosmic Debris was born. In his Santa Cruz garage (and later an artist warehouse in San Francisco) Reger created the designs, and with Matt Reed brought them into the fashion world by creating t-shirt designs that captured the essence of this mysterious young girl with 4 black cats. Since then, Cosmic</span>
  <span id="freeText17480271672416818897" style="display:none">Reger's friend Nathan Carrico designed Emily in 1991 for a skateboard company in Santa Cruz, where Cosmic Debris was born. In his Santa Cruz garage (and later an artist warehouse in San Francisco) Reger created the designs, and with Matt Reed brought them into the fashion world by creating t-shirt designs that captured the essence of this mysterious young girl with 4 black cats. Since then, Cosmic Debris has grown into a multi-million dollar firm with dozens of employees.<br /><br />Cosmic Debris has most recently moved its operations to Berkeley, California, and plans to open an Emily retail store there soon. With the momentum of mainstream success, several comics about Emily have also been made. Key creative people over the years (designers, graphic artists, illustrators), who have worked with Reger's Cosmic Debris design house are Buzz Parker, Brian Brooks, Grace Fontaine, Liz Baca, Noel Tolentino, Fawn Gehweiler, Jessica Gruner, Adele Pedersen and Nicomi "Nix" Turner. Rob Reger remains the key creative force behind the brand, and Buzz Parker is the key illustrator for the comic books and website.</span>
